The Land Bureau Is Actively Collecting Upper and Lower Season Land Tax

Collection Scheduled to Begin on August 1st

Public Notice to Inform All City Residents

The Municipal Land Bureau issued a public notice yesterday regarding the scheduled collection of the upper and lower season land tax for all districts of the city starting on August 1st. The notice stated: "For the matter of the public notice, the joint collection of the upper and lower season land tax in various districts of the city has been approved by the Municipal Government for implementation. The collection of the season tax for the nineteenth year of the Republic of China is now scheduled to begin on August 1st. The tax for this season is as follows: 1.5 yuan of regular tax silver per tael, 0.25 yuan of municipal surtax silver, 0.3 yuan of local surtax silver, and 0.123 yuan of handling fee silver. In addition, various surcharges, collectively known as the municipal administration expenses, will still be collected per mu as before and will be listed separately in the grain certificate. From the date of collection, there will be a two-month deadline for payment. If the payment is not completed within the deadline, a surcharge of 20% will be added. If the payment is still not completed after another two-month extension, a surcharge of 10% will be added as a penalty for late payment. Furthermore, the bureau has taken over the collection of land tax from the counties of Shanghai and Baoshan that have been incorporated into the city. For the fees in the former Baoshan County, there has been no distribution of separate receipts in the past, and there has been no inconvenience for the people to pay grain. The districts in the former Shanghai County originally had separate receipts. Now, after deliberation by the Bureau Affairs Meeting, it has been decided to abolish them as well, starting from this season's tax, in order to unify the system. All property owners who are required to pay new tax should pay at the counter based on the latest grain certificate. In addition to reporting to the Municipal Government and notifying them separately, this public notice is hereby issued to inform the people of the city. It is necessary to pay taxes as an obligation of the people. All property owners who are required to pay the season tax and various surcharges must complete the payment within the time limit, obtain the grain certificate, and settle their business. Do not hesitate to wait and see. This notice is of utmost importance."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests the Abolition of Duplicate Taxes

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, due to the fact that the tax collection agencies in Zhejiang Province repeatedly levied taxes on cotton fabrics approved by the Ministry of Finance, telegraphed the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Government yesterday, requesting their abolition. The original text stated: "To the Nanjing Ministry of Finance: On the 21st of this month, a letter from the silk-mercerized cotton fabric industry association in this city stated that the cotton fabric business has been declining in recent years. Since last winter, nearly half of the businesses have gone bankrupt, and most of the existing factories are also on the verge of collapse. The harsh taxes and miscellaneous levies in various provinces are increasing day by day. Recently, a letter from the Yongjia Silk and Cloth Industry Association in Zhejiang Province stated that the various sub-bureaus and enforcement offices are obstructing and levying taxes on imported local cloth. Even if there are registered certificates, the Bureau of Cloth says that there is no express written order for tax exemption, and it is difficult to take effect. They still obstruct and levy taxes. After all the businesses debated with them, they were finally allowed to temporarily record the amount of tax to be paid within one month. If the Finance Office still does not have an explicit tax exemption document by August 10, it will collect the full amount from each business, etc. Please forward it to the Ministry of Finance and strictly order the Finance Office to order all tax offices to exempt all duplicate levies, except for the payment of regular surtax at the first customs office when exporting, according to the regulations, etc., and attach a comparative table of surcharge amounts to the meeting. According to the nature of silk-mercerized cotton fabrics, they are all machine-made imitations of foreign-style goods. The registered certificate mentioned in the original letter refers to the certificate approved by the Ministry to exempt duplicate levies. Cotton textile factories of this type are opened in Shanghai. According to the regulations, they only need to pay the regular surtax at the first customs office in Shanghai when exporting. After that, holding the waybill, they can travel throughout the country and be exempted from duplicate levies. This has been a common practice for decades. The Zhejiang tax bureau actually said that there is no explicit written order for tax exemption. It is shocking that the management of the tax affairs is so ignorant of national laws. Currently, the cases of Dafeng and the First Textile Factory in Hankou being illegally and repeatedly levied taxes by Zhejiang Province have been repeatedly requested for investigation and have not yet been resolved. Furthermore, similar incidents have occurred in silk-mercerized cotton factories in this city. If this is said to promote domestic goods, it is like going south by driving the chariot north, and the result is friendship. It is appropriate to telegraph your ministry to verify and inform the Zhejiang Finance Office to strictly order the tax bureau to handle matters in accordance with the regulations and immediately abolish the practice of repeated levies, so as to maintain a glimmer of hope for the fabric factory. It is in the public interest. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce." The telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government was roughly the same (omitted).

The Red Cross to Hold a General Assembly in the Next Term

According to the Guowen News Agency, at the general assembly of the Chinese Red Cross on April 24, Wang Yiting, Wang Zhengting, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Peiyuan, Yan Huiqing, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Yongming, Wen Lanting, Liu Hongsheng, Lin Kanghou, Guan Jiongzhi, Yu Youren, Zhu Qinglan, Tai Xiling, Nie Yuntai, Di Chuqing, Chen Bingqian, Yan Fuqing, Yin Cuihe, Ye Gongchuo, Zheng Hongnian, Shi Liangcai, Wang Boqi, Rong Zongjing, Yao Yuqin, Tan Rongpu, Huang Hanzhi, Yuan Ludeng, Bei Songsun, Cai Tinggan, Tang Shaoyi, Du Yuesheng, Gu Zhuxuan, Xu Shiying, Chen Jiageng, Yang Xiaochuan, Wu Kaisheng, Shen Zhuowu, Li Cishan, Ji Heqin, Jiang Lianqiu, and dozens of others were elected as standing councilors. However, during the voting, it suddenly changed again, and 49 people were still voted for, and it was noted on the votes that it was a re-election. Hu Hongji, a representative sent by the National Government, and Wang Yansong, a representative sent by the Municipal Party Department, supervised the election. Hu Hongji and others then refused to count the votes and left. Members and others repeatedly appealed to the National Government, and the National Government ordered the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau to investigate the perpetrators. Shen Laisen, a member of the re-election committee, was arrested by the Special Zone Court for destroying the Red Cross in another case. The old standing council believed that such disputes were not good for the Red Cross, so it sent a letter to the branch associations, deciding to hold a temporary representative assembly on August 10 to resolve the election and all other issues.

The Executive Yuan's Order on the Standard for Milling Brown Rice

Must Not Be Lower Than 75%

And Must Be Higher Than 85%

The Executive Yuan of the National Government, seeing the food panic of the people, has specially stipulated the standard for milling brown rice. Its order to the Shanghai Municipal Government states: "(Omitted above) This year, the whole country is suffering from food shortages. Since this month, it has been the time of year when the crops from the previous year have run out and the new crops have not yet been harvested. The future of the people's food supply is deeply worrying. In all rice-producing areas, brown rice is milled into refined white rice, which is commonly called 'machine-milled rice.' This type of rice grain can only be milled to seven斗 from one stone of brown rice. This is an extreme waste of natural resources and a damage to the people's food supply. Investigating the milling of brown rice into coarsely milled rice, compared with machine-milled rice, can yield one more 斗, and it is still clean and smooth. If this is done, ten stone of brown rice can yield one stone of white rice. One stone of rice is enough for a family of eight for a month. This will benefit the people's food supply. The standard for milling rice grains has now been stipulated. It must not be lower than 75% and must be higher than 85% to save resources and enrich the people's food supply."

Foreign Rice Arrives Vigorously

Indica Rice Import Price Plummets

Due to the sunny and hot weather in recent days, a large amount of foreign indica rice has been imported. In addition, the production in Saigon and other places is abundant. Therefore, the import price has fallen again and again. Recently, the indica rice entering the market has fallen from around 17.5 yuan to around 14-5 yuan. It is expected that it will continue to fall within the day. There is hope that the price of rice will fall.

The Gold Standard Monetary System Law Has Been Published

Regarding the issue of gold being expensive and silver being cheap, and the method of unifying the national monetary system, the local Industry and Commerce Visiting Bureau previously collected materials, compiled them into a book and published them. It has now been proofread and published, including three volumes in Chinese, English, and Chinese-English bilingual editions. It is named "Draft Law on China's Gradual Adoption of the Gold Standard Monetary System." The bureau specially presented five copies of the published sample, along with each version, to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The ministry considered that the content of this book contained detailed information on the gold standard and the monetary system law, which was very clear. Yesterday, the ministry ordered the bureau to print hundreds of additional copies for distribution to various agencies for reference.

Yesterday's News of the Pootung Nichihua Cotton Mill Strike

The Factory Refuses Mediation

The Labor's Attitude Is Firm

The Nichihua Cotton Mill in Pootung has been on strike for three days. If the factory refuses to comply, other factories will also deny it. Therefore, if the Nichihua strike is not resolved properly this time, it will trigger a huge strike in Pootung. Detailed Account of the Municipal Finance Bureau's Crackdown on a Superstitious Donation and Fake Organization

Finance Bureau's Report on the Crackdown Process

Requesting the Public Security Bureau to Vigorously Arrest the Principal Offender

A fake organization collecting superstitious "confession" donations was discovered in Lannidu, Pudong. The Municipal Finance Bureau's South District Tax Collection Office, in conjunction with the Third District Public Security Bureau, seized privately made seals and documents and multiple fake organization staff members, who were handed over to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. These details were reported previously. Now, we have learned that the Municipal Finance Bureau's South District Tax Collection Office has submitted a detailed report on the crackdown process to the Finance Bureau. Regarding the matter of organizing superstitious "sutra repentance" donations, the Bureau had previously received repeated applications from merchant Zhang Youshi to handle the project. This was forwarded to the Municipal Government for instructions and was ordered to be postponed. This decision was communicated to Zhang Youshi. Now, according to the report from the South District Tax Collection Office, Zhang Youshi, without awaiting approval for the superstitious "sutra repentance" donation, dared to privately establish a collection organization, fraudulently obtaining money. This was extremely illegal. The Bureau immediately sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, instructing them to interrogate and investigate the apprehended individuals, including Lu Hai, and ordered them to vigorously arrest Zhang Youshi and bring him to justice. At the same time, the Bureau submitted a report to the Municipal Government regarding the circumstances of the crackdown. A summary of the facts regarding the South District Tax Collection Office's destruction of this case is extracted as follows: On the 18th of this month, the Tax Collection Office discovered in Pudong a document signed by Zhong Yuan, the "Director of the South District Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's Superstitious 'Sutra Repentance' Donation Collection Office," appointing Zhong Huidin as the "Chief Inspector." This was deeply puzzling, as the suppression of "sutra repentance" and the elimination of superstition, although previously proposed for donation collection, had never been implemented. Now, someone dared to privately establish an organization, forge documents, and fraudulently use the name of the Finance Bureau to recruit staff and parade around, which was extremely audacious. The Office dispatched clerk Cheng Fengyun, along with the stationed Tax Collection Patrol Leader Cheng Yushu, to thoroughly investigate the location of this fake organization. A letter was prepared and sent to the relevant police district, requesting police assistance. Clerk Cheng, accompanied by Patrol Leader Cheng Yushu, immediately went to various locations in Pudong in plain clothes to investigate. They found two Western-style buildings at No. 5 Lannidu Road, with two long strips of white paper pasted on either side of the door, one reading "Shanghai Finance Bureau Superstitious 'Sutra Repentance' Donation South District Preparatory Branch" and the other "Same Style Pudong District Preparatory Branch." Upon inspection, several inspectors were found inside. According to accountant Lu Hai, both branch directors were Zhong Yuan, from Fenghua County, Zhejiang, who was currently at the head office on official business. The office had been rented since the first month of the lunar year and had been preparing for several months but had not yet begun collecting donations. He claimed to be unaware of the details. Upon further questioning, inspectors Yao Yinxing, Chen Shengrong, Chen Jinlian, Huang Jiachang, Chen Diechu, Li Guowu, Zhu Daohui, Wang Zhidin, and others, mostly from Ningbo, Taizhou, and other places, claimed to have paid "movement fees" of one hundred yuan, fifty yuan, and forty yuan, respectively. Except for Lu Hai, who had been preparing with Zhong Yuan for a long time, most of them had been hired in early July and lived upstairs. In addition, there were Zhong Huidin, Zhu Daoxun, Luo Youcai, Li Guowen, Wang Yunchuang, and more than ten others who were said to be out and not yet returned. Upstairs, two rooms were used as dormitories for the staff. Downstairs, two rooms were used as offices. Zhong Yuan's wife, Zhong Ying, and children lived in the back room. Zhong Ying then claimed that her husband, Zhong Yuan, had paid more than seven hundred yuan to the "head office" and had already spent it all. She produced two "appointment letters" from the so-called "head office," namely Zhang Youshi, "Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau's Superstitious 'Sutra Repentance' Donation Collection Office," appointing Zhong Yuan as the "Director of the South District and Pudong District." There was also a copy of the "Shanghai Special Municipality Superstition Donation Collection Regulations." When asked where the "head office" was located, they claimed that the office had recently moved and was only known to be located in the Baoshan Road and Yongxing Road area of Zhabei, but the exact address was unknown. Clerk Cheng and others, after interrogating them, feared that they might be nervous and attempt to escape. Therefore, Patrol Leader Cheng Yushu was assigned to temporarily guard them, while they went to the First District to deliver a letter, requesting District Chief Zhang to send police assistance. Police Officer Tong was dispatched with four policemen to search the premises. In addition to all the furniture and other items in the house, an inventory was made, and the police were left to guard them. The seals of the Pudong Public Office and account books of bribery money were also copied, along with Zhong Ying, Lu Hai, and a total of ten people, and taken to the district for investigation. During the interrogation, Zhong Yuan was apprehended and brought to the district by the patrol police. According to his statement, he did not know the truth of the matter and placed all the responsibility on Zhang Youshi, who falsely claimed to be the Director of the head office. Later, District Chief Zhang of the Third District requested instructions from Bureau Chief Yuan. Zhong Yuan and the ten other men and women were sent to the Bureau for interrogation.

An Appeal from Hanzhong, Shaanxi

The Shanghai Foreign Charity Relief Association received a letter yesterday from Chinese and foreign members of the Foreign Relief Association in Hanzhong, Shaanxi, appealing for aid. The letter is excerpted as follows: "Since 1927, Hanzhong has suffered disasters every year, and last year, the drought was particularly severe. From spring to autumn, there was no rain at all, and all vegetation withered. The five grains failed to produce any crops, and even the mountains and marshes were exhausted, making drinking water difficult to find. Afterwards, heavy snow fell, and we hoped for a prosperous year, but the extreme cold was unprecedented. The disaster victims have no food to eat and no clothes to keep warm, resulting in countless deaths of disaster victims and livestock. The situation is even worse this spring. Those who relied on grass roots and tree bark to survive have quickly run out of these as well. The so-called 'bare walls' families have already sold even those walls. The city and the fields are filled with starving people, and all that can be heard is the crying of hunger and cold. The dead are piled up, and there is no time to bury them. The foul air is breeding epidemics, and it is estimated that more than a thousand people are dying every day. The main agricultural products of Hanzhong are rice and corn. This spring, seven or eight out of ten people have lost their seeds and have nothing to plant, so there is no hope for an autumn harvest. The situation is unimaginable. The most severely affected areas in the Hanzhong disaster area include the entire counties of Lueyang, Fengxian, Mianxian, Ningqiang, Yangxian, and Xixiang, as well as the northwest areas of Nanzheng and Chenggu counties, and the northeast, west, and northwest areas of Baocheng. The other areas of Nancheng and Baocheng, as well as the counties of Zhenba, Foping, and Liuba, are slightly less affected. In addition, all counties under Ankang are likely to be affected by the drought. It is estimated that there are more than two million disaster victims waiting for relief. Due to the rugged mountain roads, inconvenient transportation, and the time required for postal and telegraphic communication, the news has been delayed, resulting in charitable individuals investigating and distributing relief not arriving. Our Association is pleading for the people until our voices are hoarse, and we have finally obtained a relief fund of 10,000 yuan from your Association. However, at this critical moment of life and death, this is just a drop in the bucket. We hope that all charitable individuals will embrace a sense of equality and perform acts of generous giving and universal salvation. If you raise any further relief funds, please distribute them equally to Hanzhong and remit them quickly so that we can promptly take action to provide emergency relief to alleviate the suffering and implement long-term relief to benefit the source of the disaster. Do not let the more than two million starving and desperate people suffer the tragedy of being turned away without relief."

Local News 2

Lu Genrong's Release on Bail

Applying for Bail Out of Custody Following Precedent

Court Interrogation of Various Circumstances

Tang Weizhi Provides a Guarantee of Fifty Yuan

Lu Will Come to Shanghai to Seek a Living

Suzhou Express Mail: After Lu Genrong was granted permission to be released from custody, he entrusted the Rongxing Tobacco and Paper Shop in Pingqiao yesterday (the 23rd) to provide a written guarantee of fifty yuan and submitted it to the High Court for release from prison. The original text of this petition is attached below:

Criminal Petition Petitioner: Lu Genrong, regarding a case that has been judged and declared innocent, but the plaintiff official has appealed and the case has not been finalized, requests to be released from custody pending trial following precedent. Since the petitioner was detained on June 24th of the lunar calendar in the 17th year of the Republic for being accused of enticement and theft, the case has been repeatedly tried and sent back for retrial twice by the Supreme Court, lasting for two years. Fortunately, the court has now declared him innocent in the second retrial. He deeply hopes to regain his freedom soon. However, the plaintiff official filed an appeal during the period before the judgment was finalized. However, only Article 1, Section 1, Clause 3 of the Regulations on Detaining Defendants in Civil and Criminal Cases, promulgated by the President on September 13th, 1921, stipulates that those who have been judged and declared innocent, even if the plaintiff or prosecutor appeals, should be released pending trial. This regulation is listed in the laws and regulations of the National Government, promulgated by the late Premier in the Guangdong government, and is naturally still valid. Furthermore, the petitioner's suspected crimes, except for the enticement portion, which has been dismissed, the plaintiff official also acknowledges that there are no issues with the aiding and abetting theft portion. The plaintiff official's argument for appeal only mentions a slight suspicion of transporting stolen goods, which is not among the offenses with the lightest principal punishment of five years or more of imprisonment. The petitioner has parents who can be entrusted with his care, and Wu Ta has a fixed residence. Regarding the witnesses and evidence in this case, they have been thoroughly investigated in previous trials, and none of the circumstances listed in Articles 41 to 43 of Article 66 of the Criminal Procedure Law apply. There is no conflict with the provisions of Article 6 of the aforementioned regulation promulgated by the late Premier. Furthermore, the court has approved the release on bail of many defendants who have been declared innocent in cases where the plaintiff official has filed appeals that have not yet been finalized. The petitioner should also receive the same treatment. Therefore, this petition is submitted, requesting the court to examine and approve it, and to check the provisions of Clause 3 of Section 1 of Article 1 of the aforementioned regulations, as well as the precedents for bailing out defendants in cases pending appeal, and to grant release pending trial, in order to comply with the legislative spirit of the late Premier and to uphold the court's authority in treating all equally, so that the petitioner can avoid further detention and await the Supreme Court's third judgment. We respectfully request an immediate ruling for implementation. Respectfully submitted to the Jiangsu High Court.

Another letter: Yesterday (the 23rd), after Lu Genrong received the ruling, he commissioned lawyer Song Mingxun to draft a bail bond and stated that he was unable to raise the cash bail at this time and requested written bail. Lawyer Song submitted the petition to the High Court at 8:00 AM, and Judge Zhao approved it and immediately signed a ticket ordering the police at the Jiangsu Third Prison Substation on Hengjie Street, Wuxian County, to bring Lu Genrong to the court. Lu's cousin, Tang Weizhi, provided the guarantee. At 12:00 PM, Judge Zhao Zhengcheng, accompanied by clerk Xu Heng, took his seat in the Third Court, brought Lu Genrong and ordered the guarantor Tang Weizhi to appear in court. He first asked Lu Genrong if he wanted to apply for bail. (Answer) Yes. (Question) Did you receive the ruling yesterday? (Answer) Yes. (Question) The ruling stated that a cash guarantee of fifty yuan was required, but why couldn't you raise it and wanted to change it to a written guarantee? (Answer) Because I can't think of a way. My family is also very poor, and I have been in prison for two years. I really can't think of a way. (Question) What is your relationship with Tang Weizhi? (Answer) He is a friend of my father. (Instruction) Your case has already been finalized, but because the prosecutor has filed an appeal, your innocence is still uncertain, so you are required to post bail. But after you go out, you must behave yourself and not do such things again. (Answer) I dare not. (Question) I heard that after you go out, you want to file a lawsuit against Zhihua Hospital to demand compensation from Huang Yongnian. Is this true? (Answer) This was just a thought while in prison. (Instruction) Don't create any more problems after you go out. If you are summoned, you must appear promptly. (Answer) Of course. He then questioned Tang Weizhi, who stated that he was thirty-six years old and from Nanbeiqiao, Wuxian County. (Question) What shop are you guaranteeing? (Answer) Rongxing Tobacco and Paper Shop on Shizijie Street. (Question) How much capital does Rongxing have? (Answer) One or two thousand yuan. (Question) What position do you hold there? (Answer) I am the manager. (Question) Do you know the responsibility you are guaranteeing? (Answer) Yes. (Question) What responsibility do you know? (Answer) If Lu Genrong is summoned in the future, he will appear promptly. Tang Weizhi immediately submitted a guarantee letter stating: "I, Tang Weizhi, hereby guarantee that Lu Genrong will be on bail in Suzhou City under the criminal court of the Jiangsu High Court, and will appear whenever summoned. If he fails to appear when summoned, all the guarantee money of fifty yuan will be forfeited to the guarantor's willingness to pay immediately as ordered. If he fails to pay, he is willing to be subject to compulsory execution. This guarantee letter is made in accordance with Article 75, Section 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law. Tang Weizhi (signed), July 23, 1930." After receiving the guarantee letter, Judge Zhao immediately ordered Lu Genrong's release in court. After Lu Genrong was released from the court, he returned to his hometown with his cousin Tang Weizhi on the same day. Lu stated that he would go to Shanghai to find business in the near future.

Tong Sanmao Sentenced to Two Years

Huang Baiying Did Not Appear in Person Yesterday

Sanmao Still Prepares to Appeal

The sensational case of the dancer Huang Baiying being forced to take poison has been ongoing for more than twenty days. The court has held three hearings on the case, and the details have been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday morning was the date for the pronouncement of the verdict in the case. The authorities of the Special District Local Court, in view of the previous crowding of the audience and the lack of legal means to prevent it, ordered two bailiffs in advance yesterday morning to stand guard at the entrance of the Second Court after 7:00 AM. When they saw that the audience seats in the courtroom were full, they prohibited outsiders from entering the court. Although the number of people who went to listen yesterday was not as large as before, all the seats were already occupied before 8:00 AM. The plaintiff, Huang Baiying, did not appear in person and was represented by her lawyer, Zhang Yuanmei. The police lawyer, Bo Liang, Li Zhishan, and the lawyer Zou Yu, who was appointed by the court to defend the defendant, all attended one after another. At 8:40 AM, Judge Wu Tingqi, Prosecutor Xu Mei, and the clerk came to the court and took their seats. The bailiff was ordered to bring the defendant, Tong Sanmao (i.e., Tong Wenbo), from the waiting room and place him in the defendant's position. Tong was still wearing the suit he had worn during the previous interrogation. Judge Wu first asked him for his name and age, then stood up and read out the main text of the judgment: The defendant Tong Sanmao is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for the crime of inciting attempted murder. The number of days in detention before the judgment is determined will be counted as two days to offset one day of imprisonment. After the judgment was pronounced, the bailiff escorted Tong back to the police station to await execution after the judgment is finalized. At that time, Tong did not express his dissatisfaction with the imprisonment in court, but it was heard that he still intends to appeal.

Service Was Briefly Suspended Due to Flooding but Has Now Resumed

Li Senfu Escapes Danger

First Hidden in a Thatched Hut in Beixinjing

Then Moved to a Rural Area in the Sun Temple Township

Treatment in the Bandit's Den Was Not Bad

Li Only Managed to Escape and Return Yesterday Morning

Li Senfu, manager of the Jiucheng Second Silk Reeling Factory in Rihuigang, Tapuqiao, Nanshi, was kidnapped on the morning of the 17th of this month at 7:00 AM while traveling from his home at No. 15 Xinyili, Xujiahui Road, to the factory in his own chauffeured car. Three kidnappers suddenly appeared and abducted Li without a trace. The details have been reported in this newspaper. We now learn that Li escaped from the bandit's den yesterday morning at 4:00 AM. It is said that after Li was kidnapped, he was directly hidden in a thatched hut in Beixinjing. The next evening, he was moved to a bungalow in the rural Sun Temple township in Zhabei. The house was surrounded by bamboo fences. He was treated well for the first two days, and on the first day, he was even served domino-brand ham and steamed chicken and other delicacies. The surveillance was not very strict, and he was not ordered to send a letter to his family. The bandits sent a letter directly to Li's residence and once contacted him in Tanziwan, Zhabei. The day before yesterday, Li's residence received another letter from the bandits, and the location was scheduled for negotiations on Wusong Road. Undercover detectives disguised themselves and went there, but after waiting all night, no one from the bandits came. At the same time, Li took advantage of the bandits' fatigue and sleep and escaped alone. He went to a friend's house first and returned home at 9:00 AM. He immediately moved his whole family away, leaving only two maids to guard the house.

The Hull of the Sunken Kangtai Steamer Will Be Blown Up Today

The evening newspaper reports that the Kangtai Steamer collided with the Italian ship Libya in the Wusongkou on March 26th of last year and sank. The Jianghai Customs and the Tokyo Salvage Company signed a contract to carry out the salvage work, which lasted for two months. This morning (the 23rd), according to the Mitsui Company, the resident manager of the company in Shanghai, all the items and equipment in the ship have been salvaged, but the hull is completely flooded and firmly embedded in the mud, making it difficult to lift. Moreover, carrying out this work will inevitably hinder ships entering the port. Therefore, it has been agreed with the Kangtai Steamer Company to destroy it with explosives, which is scheduled to be carried out on Thursday afternoon. The Kangtai Steamer Company only had this one ship, and it has ceased operations since it was sunk.

Zhang Maocheng Rice Shop to Sell Rice at Cost

Zhang Maocheng Rice Shop on Haining Road has always adhered to the principle of low profits and open business practices. It was the first to create a system of posted prices, which it has maintained for more than ten years. Now, considering the high rice prices and the difficult lives of the people, the owner has personally gone to various places to purchase rice, regardless of cost. Starting from July 25th of the lunar calendar, various types of rice will be sold at cost until rice prices stabilize. However, the shop believes that its scope is small and its resources are limited, and it hopes that other enthusiastic members of the industry will follow suit and jointly support this righteous cause, so that the majority of civilians in Shanghai can benefit. The rice prices for the cost sale are as follows: Special grade white rice is 20 yuan per stone, second grade white rice is 19 yuan per stone, special grade Yangjian rice is 16 yuan per stone, second grade Yangjian rice is 14 yuan 8 jiao per stone. Each stone weighs 200 pounds, and each person is limited to one stone. The hours are from 7:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM daily.

News from the Yangjing Town Epidemic Prevention Clinic

Li Zhonghua Detained for Eight Months

Silk merchant Chen Liangsheng repeatedly received threatening letters, so he reported to the Seventh Team of the Security Corps, which dispatched platoon leader Jin Shunchang, team member Gu Guoyou, etc., to arrest at the location of Xiaozha Bridge. Li Zhonghua, a Hebei native also known as Li Zhongyi, arrived at the destination and used the method on his threatening letter, and was arrested by Jin and others. Because he attempted to escape and resisted, he was shot in the wrist. Afterwards, Li Zhonghua counter-sued the Security Corps for murder. After investigation by the local court, the Security Corps members were found not guilty, and Li Zhonghua was detained and prosecuted. The final debate was held the day before yesterday, and yesterday morning, Judge Shen opened the court to pronounce the verdict. After questioning Li Zhonghua's age and origin, the court announced that Li Zhonghua, also known as Li Zhongyi, was found guilty of attempted extortion and sentenced to six months of imprisonment; he was found guilty of exploiting exorbitant interest rates and sentenced to four months of imprisonment. The sentences would be served concurrently for a total of eight months. The number of days detained before the final judgment would be counted, with two days of detention offsetting one day of imprisonment. The three threatening letters and the four loan sharking account books were all confiscated. After the announcement, he was warned that this was a lenient sentence, and that he should not lend money at usurious rates in the future, nor should he engage in illegal activities. He was asked if he accepted the judgment, and Li replied that he did. The judge then ordered him to sign the record and be taken down to be sent to prison.

Zhou Zhanhong and Two Others Acquitted After Appeal

Gao Jieren, the owner of the Tongfa firm and a broker at the Yarn and Cloth Exchange, accused his partners Zhou Zhanhong, Chen Luping, and Tao Jiyuan of embezzling 160,000 yuan in funds. A verdict had already been issued, sentencing Zhou to eight months of imprisonment and Chen and Tao to two months of imprisonment each. The three men did not accept the verdict and appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court. The court has now concluded its trial, and yesterday morning, Judge Song and Assessors Du and Ye opened the court to pronounce the verdict. Zhou, Chen, and Tao were all found not guilty, and Gao Jieren's attached civil suit was dismissed.

Decision Imminent in Detectives' Appeal Case

Cao Jie, a detective of the Hongkou Police Station, and detectives Xu Wenzhong and Chen Bingsheng, previously detained Hu Changbao, a Jiangbei native who dealt in yellow sand and gravel, on suspicion of theft. After investigation revealed that the suspicion was unfounded, he was released without prosecution. However, Chen Zhi, the adoptive father of Hu Changbao, who was released, gave Cao and others 250 yuan as a thank-you gift. Although Cao and others refused to accept it, the matter was reported to their superiors, and they were charged with accepting bribes. The case has already been concluded by the Wu District Local Court. In addition to Chen Zhi being sentenced to two months of imprisonment, Cao, Xu, and Chen were each sentenced to two and a half years of imprisonment and fined. Detailed information has been reported previously. However, Cao and the other three, along with Chen Zhi, were not satisfied with the first-instance judgments and each hired a lawyer to submit a statement, stating their reasons and appealing to the Jiangsu Higher Court, requesting that the original judgment be overturned and that they be declared innocent. Yesterday morning, Judge Song of the Criminal Court and Assessors Du and Gao of the court specially opened the First Court, summoned witnesses, and ordered the appellants to be brought forward to be interrogated one by one. The testimonies of all parties were largely the same as in the first instance. After the debate was concluded, the court ordered Zhao and others to be returned to custody and to await a scheduled verdict.

Young Child Dashes Across Street, Dies Tragically

No Blame Attributed to Driver

Father Collects Body in Tears

Dr. Elie Grem, the day before yesterday, was riding in car number 7248, driven by his hired Chinese driver Gu Houyi, driving north from the southern end of the Bund. When passing the Renji Road intersection, two young children suddenly dashed across from the Huangpu River towards Renji Road. The child in front safely reached the intersection, but the child following behind, named Xie Shanzhi, was struck by the car when he was in the middle of the road. He was immediately injured and lost consciousness. He was rushed to Renji Hospital by a policeman, but the injuries were fatal and he died shortly afterwards. The hospital notified the General Police Station, which sent detectives to take the child's body to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the corpse's father Xie Zhaoji and the driver Gu Houyi were summoned to the morgue. Subsequently, the Special District Local Court appointed Prosecutor Guo to come to the morgue for an examination. According to a report from the Western police chief, after arriving at the scene of the accident and investigating the situation, he stated that the incident was not the fault of the driver. However, the corpse's father, Xie Zhaoji, claimed that his son was still far away from the car at the time, and the driver could have stopped or avoided him, but the driver continued to drive wildly, causing the accident. Gu Houyi testified that the deceased was not careful when walking and that it had nothing to do with him. Prosecutor Guo then ordered Xie to sign a guarantee to collect the body for burial and stated that according to the police investigation, the incident was not the fault of the driver and that no prosecution should be initiated. If the corpse's father had more detailed evidence at the time, he would be allowed to file a lawsuit himself. Xie, upon hearing this, signed the guarantee in tears and collected the body for burial.

The Shanghai South Public Bus number three was being driven into the depot by the driver Shan Asi the other night when it carelessly hit Xu Atu, who was relaxing by the roadside in Lujiabang, breaking his leg. The policeman on duty arrested Shan and took him to the Second District Police Station. He was handed over to the local court for questioning yesterday.

Extortion by Gangsters Continues Unabated

Huge Sums Already Paid

Trying to Extort Again

Detectives Arrest Two

Admit to Extortion

Ni Baofu, the manager, and Tang Liangzhen, the assistant manager of the Sanyang South Goods Store on Nanjing Road, suddenly received a threatening letter with a bullet attached in June of last year, extorting money. Ni and others initially ignored it, but the gang was determined to get the money and continued to send threatening letters. Ni and others received more than twenty letters in total. Because they did not want to make an issue of it, they kept it secret and never announced it to the public. They only sent someone to contact the bandits and paid them seven times, totaling 746 yuan. The gang then stopped harassing them. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday afternoon, a tea server named Yu Ade from a certain hotel sent a letter to Sanyang, wanting Ni Baofu to receive it. However, Ni had already left Shanghai for the summer due to the hot weather. After the store staff read it, they realized that it was another letter from the threatening gang. They followed the instructions, put 100 yuan in banknotes into a longan package, and handed it back to Yu to take back. The store clerk Gui Quanxiang accompanied Yu to a room number 318 in the certain hotel. At that time, there was no one in the room. Gui also entered the room, saying that he had to wait for a face-to-face meeting. After a while, a man came in casually and turned around to leave after seeing Gui's face. Gui immediately chased after him and followed him to the vicinity of the Zhejiang Road vegetable market, where there was a Chinese police post number 1010. Gui called the police, who intercepted the escaping man and took him back to the Lao Zha Police Station. The man was identified as Kong Shaotang from Jiangning. Kong admitted that he wrote the letter and also named his accomplice Gu Weixin from Chongming, who was inside the Zikang South Goods Store at number 149 Ximen Road. The head of the patrol Liu Chunshu and Wang Shusen rushed to arrest Gu. Yesterday morning, he and Kong were handed over to the Special District Local Court. Judge Zhou brought them in for questioning. The police lawyer briefly described the case and requested a postponement because further investigation was needed. When questioned, Kong still admitted to writing the threatening letter, but Gu denied the crime. The court ordered Kong and Gu to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Her husband's sister interfered and accused her of abuse, causing her to become angry and jump into the river to end her life. Her family member, Shen Jinfu, was summoned and took her away.

Rescued Too Late in the Dark

Investigating the Deceased's Family

At around 10 p.m. the night before last, a well-dressed middle-aged man walked alone to the China Merchants Bureau Fei Ke launch at the Fourth Road pier and lingered. The sailors initially suspected that he was cooling off, so they did not suspect him. Unexpectedly, the man suddenly took off a light green moire silk gauze robe and a soft straw hat that he was wearing and threw them onto the launch when people were not paying attention, and then jumped into the river to commit suicide. By the time the sailors on the launch heard the sound and urgently tried to rescue him, it was already dark and he was nowhere to be found. Chinese constables number 1447 and 2830 were informed and took the man's clothing and hat to the Central Police Station. Since the case occurred on the water, the Water Patrol Police Station was notified by telegraph, and Patrolman Cheng Yongnian went to take the clothing and hat away and temporarily stored them at the police station in order to identify the deceased's family for identification.

Man and Woman Both Commit Suicide by Poisoning

Han Qinying A 19-year-old woman from Wuxi, Han Qinying, lived upstairs in the Yongxiangtai wood shop on Edward Road. Her husband, Zhou Renjie, worked at the Yarn and Cloth Exchange. A few days ago, Zhou's mother-in-law sent a letter from her hometown saying that she had 200 yuan and would entrust a fellow villager to bring it to Shanghai in the near future, and asked them to check and receive it. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday (the 22nd), a fellow villager came to their house and told Qin Ying that the money had been robbed on the way. At that time, Qin Ying borrowed a telephone to call Renjie, only saying that the fellow villager had come home, but did not mention the robbery. When Zhou finished work and returned home, he learned that the money had been lost and was extremely frustrated. He had a quarrel with his wife Qin Ying, and Zhou left in a daze. The woman became depressed and had a sudden suicidal thought. She swallowed a full pipe of raw opium at around 9:00 PM that night. She was discovered and taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, but she died at 10:00 AM the next morning due to an overdose of poison.

Adopted Daughter-in-Law Repeatedly Lured and Abducted for Rape

Huang Dejun, 46 years old, from Taizhou, who runs a stove shop at number 28 Xiqingnianhui Lane, Caojiadu, Shanghai West, has a son named Ruxi, who is just over 20 years old. He previously adopted Sheng Dunfa's daughter Yingdi (15 years old) as a child bride through a matchmaker. Later, Huang thought that his daughter-in-law was quite smart, so he asked someone to get her a job at the Toyota Yarn Factory last year. She went to work in the morning and returned in the evening, as usual. Unexpectedly, Zhang Guanglu, who lived at number 24 in the same lane, fell in love with her at first sight and coveted her. He first flirted with the woman every day, and then started to seduce her. Since this year, she has been lured and abducted for rape twice. Huang had to endure because he was no match for Zhang's power. He had already chosen an auspicious day in the eighth month to complete his son's marriage. Unexpectedly, on May 27, the daughter-in-law was suddenly lured and abducted by Zhang and hidden without a trace. Huang Dejun took Zhang to the Sixth District Police Station, which interrogated him and transferred him to the court for interrogation. Now it is known that the case has been tried several times in court, and Zhang is still detained in the institute. On the 15th of this month, Huang suddenly found the daughter-in-law near there and took her home. Only six days later, at around 8:00 PM the day before yesterday, Zhang Guanglu's old mother, Zhang Bao, went to Zhang's place on the pretext of buying water and took the daughter-in-law away when people were not paying attention. Huang chased after her, but she had disappeared without a trace. Shortly afterwards, Bao returned home. Huang reported to the Sixth District Police Station, which sent police to arrest Zhang Bao and Zhang Jingwen. After being interrogated by the district chief, Huang Dejun, the plaintiff, stated that he was 46 years old, from Taizhou, and lived at number 28 Xiqingnianhui Lane, running a stove shop. The defendant, Zhang Bao, stated that she was 49 years old, from Huizhou, and lived at number 14 Xiqingnianhui Lane. Zhang Jingwen stated that he was 62 years old and lived at the same address. The district chief, considering that the case involved luring and abduction for rape, prepared a document and handed them over to the Local Court for interrogation.

Special Item

Municipal Government Announces Rules for Citizens' Use of Shoreline

The municipal government announced yesterday the rules for citizens' use of shoreline, stating: "The Shanghai Municipal Government hereby promulgates the Rules for Citizens' Use of Shoreline. This is the order."

Shanghai Municipal Rules for Citizens' Use of Shoreline: Article 1: The waterline along the banks of all rivers in this city where ships are moored shall be called the "shoreline." Any tidal flats, whether filled or unfilled, shall not be considered part of the shoreline. Article 2: Anyone building a wharf or using the shoreline along the banks of any river in this city, regardless of whether the land or tidal flats are owned by the state, the city, private individuals, or leased, must apply to the Port Authority for a shoreline use permit. Article 3: Anyone applying for a shoreline use permit must provide the location, starting and ending points of the shoreline segment, the duration of use, and the purpose of the wharf in a written request to the Port Authority for approval. They must then find a reputable guarantor in this city and obtain a shoreline use permit and shoreline map from the Port Authority before using the shoreline. The format of the permit will be determined separately. The permit is of a long-term nature and does not need to be carried around during the Port Authority-approved period of use. Article 4: Anyone applying for a shoreline use permit must pay the following fees according to the regulations and obtain a receipt: (A) A one-time handling fee must be paid when applying for the permit: ten silver dollars for the Huangpu River shoreline, eight silver dollars for the Wusong River shoreline, and six silver dollars per year for other waterways. (B) Six months' shoreline usage fee must be prepaid, as well as a deposit equal to half of the shoreline usage fee. Article 5: The shoreline usage fee shall be collected according to the shoreline usage fee schedule established by the Municipal Government Property Evaluation Committee. In special circumstances, the Municipal Government may change the fee schedule at any time. Article 6: Shoreline users shall pay an annual usage fee, starting from the date of obtaining the shoreline usage permit. The fee shall be paid to the Port Authority in advance in two installments each year, and a receipt shall be obtained as proof of payment. If there are any arrears in payment, the deposit shall be deducted. If the deduction reaches one-half of the total deposit and the payment is still not made up, the right to use the shoreline shall be revoked, and the user shall be ordered to dismantle the wharf and other buildings completely, and the remaining deposit shall be returned. Article 7: The deposit will be refunded in full when the usage period expires, provided that there are no outstanding usage fees. Article 8: The duration of shoreline use shall be specified by the user at their discretion and submitted to the Port Authority for approval. Article 9: Shoreline users shall not transfer or sublet the permit or privately sublet part or all of the shoreline to others for use. Article 10: In addition to applying to the Public Works Bureau for a permit to build a wharf, shoreline users must first submit the length of the wharf extending into the water to the Port Authority for approval. Article 11: Any citizen who uses the shoreline without the approval of the Port Authority will, once discovered, be charged double the usage fee from the date of occupancy, and all buildings will be immediately ordered to be demolished. However, those who have already built wharves before the promulgation and implementation of these rules may apply to the Port Authority for a shoreline usage permit within one month after promulgation. Article 12: During the period of shoreline use, the Port Authority may increase the usage fee once every five years, based on the circumstances measured according to the shoreline usage fee schedule. However, the increase shall not exceed 20% of the original usage fee each time, and the user shall be notified three months in advance. Article 13: Upon receiving notification of an increase in the usage fee, shoreline users shall submit their original permit to the Port Authority for endorsement. Article 14: Repairs to embankments, dredging of mud and sand, and related expenses shall be the responsibility of the shoreline user, but they must be approved by the competent authority before construction can begin. Article 15: If a shoreline user is unable to continue paying fees due to business setbacks during the period of use, they may request the Port Authority to return the permit and cancel the right to use the shoreline, but they must pay another six months' usage fee from the date of the request. Article 16: The original shoreline user shall have the priority right to apply for a continued permit within one month after the expiration of the usage period. If the request is not continued after the deadline, the wharf and other buildings shall be dismantled, and the shoreline shall be returned. However, if the Municipal Government needs it, it may purchase the shoreline at an appraised price with the consent of the original user. Article 17: If a shoreline user uses the wharf for illegal activities or activities that harm the public interest, the Port Authority may revoke the permit at any time and confiscate the deposit. If there are any outstanding usage fees, the guarantor may be pursued for payment. Article 18: If it is necessary to use the leased shoreline for municipal facilities, such as the construction of public wharves, the Port Authority may recover all or part of the shoreline and revoke or change the permit. The wharf built by the user shall be jointly appraised by both parties, and the Port Authority shall fund the purchase. Article 19: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions. Article 20: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

Social News

Mortality Statistics of American Automobile Accidents

According to a recent report released by the U.S. Department of Commerce, automobile accidents in the United States have been increasing year by year. In 1929, a total of 31,000 people died in automobile accidents across the country, and approximately one million men, women, and children were injured. In total, 83,000 people died in automobile accidents in the two years from 1927 to 1929. From 1920 to 1929, a total of 190,850 people died. Based on a standard of 100,000 people, the accident mortality rate in 1920 was 16%, which increased to 27% in 1929 and to 93% this year. According to these results, the number of accident deaths is quickly approaching the rate of car increase.

The causes of this are (1) driver negligence, (2) poor road maintenance, (3) dim streetlights, (4) pedestrian carelessness, and (5) the development of commerce. The resulting death toll exceeds the number of American deaths during the European War. Moreover, the economic losses caused by automobile accidents in 1929 alone amounted to no less than 850 million. If we observe the number of casualties in the first four months of this year, the number will certainly increase compared to last year. The government has no good way to prevent this, and can only hope to pay attention to driving safety. (Yi Kang)

The Amount of Polluted Air Absorbed by New York City Residents

According to a report from the New York City Department of Health's Chemical Experiment Laboratory, the air is best at 4:00 AM and worst after 9:00 AM. Based on one million residents in busy streets near Central Park, each person absorbs an average of 1.35 pounds of polluted air every 15 minutes. Therefore, from January 11th to 27th of this year alone, the degree of unclean air ranged from 27% pounds to 2.7 pounds. To prevent and test the degree of air cleanliness, municipal authorities have decided to install dust-collecting paper outside each window. The paper will have 96 grids, and the degree of dust, etc., will be measured according to the weight and quality of the dust collected on the paper. It is expected that this result will be a great help in measuring the mortality rate of citizens in the future. (Yi Kang)

World Silver Production is Fourteen Times Greater Than Gold

According to a survey published by the U.S. Department of Mines, the world's silver production from 1493 to 1927 totaled 14,000,000,000 ounces, which is fourteen times more than the gold produced in the same period. This amount of silver could pave Broadway in New York City from Battery Park to Central Park (over four miles) to a height of six inches. From 1493 to 1600, the world produced 747,000,000 ounces of silver. From 1601 to 1700, the world produced 1,272,000,000 ounces of silver. From 1701 to 1800, the world produced 1,833,000,000 ounces of silver. This amount is still less than the amount produced from 1919 to 1927. From 1493 to 1880, the world produced 3,852,000,000 ounces of silver. This amount is still less than the amount produced from 1909 to 1927. More silver has been produced since 1888 than was produced from 1493 to 1887. In other words, the amount produced in 396 years is less than the amount produced in the last 39 years.

Crime in Tokyo Doubles in One Year

Tokyo Dispatch: According to statistics released by the Tokyo District Court, the number of criminals in Tokyo in the first half of this year has almost doubled compared to the same period last year. There were 1,149 minor thefts, 115 cases of malfeasance, 14 cases of rape, 10 cases of robbery, and a total of 1,458 cases of gambling.

Book and Newspaper Reviews

"Our Generation" by Xia Zhongfang

The books and newspapers reviewed in this publication are all published works. Today, I will make an exception and introduce a collection of poems that has not yet been published.

Both old and new Chinese literature have reached a state of decline, especially poetry, which has recently experienced a slump. The most accurate criticism from the Vanguard Weekly is that the literary world lacks a central consciousness. This is a very accurate assessment.

Poetry has always been considered the most beautiful flower in literature, so literature that lacks poetry is a sign of its decline. In the declining Chinese literary world, we have found a very good collection of poems, and the works in this collection all have a central consciousness. Therefore, I cannot wait for the poetry collection to be published and will introduce it first.

The first poem I want to introduce is "Our Generation" by Fang Guangming.

Sisters and brothers,

We are only fifteen or sixteen years old,

We all have strong bodies,

We all have unlimited courage,

Our China, the rivers and mountains are beautiful,

We young people, unite together,

Sisters and brothers, encourage each other,

Sisters and brothers, encourage each other,

Our great-grandparents often sighed,

For the decline of the Chinese people's livelihood,

Our fathers, our mothers,

Often shed tears for the decline of the nation,

Their era has passed,

Now it is our generation,

We will strive, following one after another,

Overthrow all international tyranny,

We love and protect the Chinese nation,

The glory of the nation will never be replaced,

Look, the national flag of the blue sky and white sun,

Sways in the wind today,

After reading this poem, we truly feel a bright future ahead of us. The "our generation" mentioned in the poem is not the generation of the person writing this review, nor the generation of the author, but refers to the next generation. Our generation is truly too pitiful. We are responsible for all the suffering and all the darkness. We hope that our next generation will not be as corrupt and degenerate as our generation.

Our author proactively, enthusiastically, and optimistically anticipates the situation of our next generation, stimulating us to work hard and sweep away the morbid and nauseating poems that were once considered interesting. This is truly worthy of everyone singing. Now, let us introduce another poem by the same author, "Welcome Forward."

Brothers, charge forward,

We are the vanguard of the Chinese nation,

Welcome forward, welcome forward,

Eliminate all reactionary forces that harm the nation,

Brothers, charge forward,

Break through the multiple oppressions of the great powers,

Welcome forward, welcome forward,

For the independence and prosperity of the nation,

Brothers, charge forward,

Let us show our bravery,

Welcome forward, welcome forward,

Our cause is grand and glorious,

We feel that in this chaotic and declining era of Chinese literature, it is appropriate to have a bolt from the blue to awaken the literary figures who are short-sighted, blindly crashing around, and locking themselves in ivory towers. At the same time, the people of the whole country also need such bright and passionate poems to inspire them. It is said that these songs are already being set to music by music composers. We hope that the sheet music can also be released soon for all the youth of China to sing together. Fang Jun's many songs, as well as the works of other authors, all have a consistent central idea, and the words and tones are all a new world in the poetry world. However, this review has already been written too long and cannot be written any further. Fortunately, the poetry collection will be printed soon, and everyone can sing their hearts out.

Oath Increases

By Chen Bocui

Of course, the Chinese poetry scene has recently been pitifully silent. The main reason for this unfavorable phenomenon is that most poets are engaged in "crude and shoddy work" and "senseless moaning," losing the principle of poetry as the highest expression of art. We feel that the unusual decline of the Chinese poetry scene is not worth lamenting. Many young poets think that writing poetry is merely a kind of literary pastime, simply moaning sadly, instead of consciously creating great poems as works of art for appreciation. Regarding this, we hold immense pessimism about the future of Chinese poetry, and also feel a chill regarding the future of young Chinese poets.

Mr. Hunt once said, "Poetry is the expression of passion for truth, beauty, and power. It concretizes its concepts, uses imagination, and adjusts language to fit the principle of diverse and unified rhythm." Applying these words to Chinese poets, it seems that very few can bear the weight without shame. Can humming a few lines about flowers, the moon, and gentle breezes while sitting on a lover's lap, or writing some senseless, seemingly poetic lines while lying on a sofa in a coffee shop, be considered poetry?

Recently, I read Chen Bocui's poem "Oath." Objectively, I feel that his poem reveals the expression of truth, beauty, and power between each line, giving me a new impression that I cannot find in other poetry collections. Whether Mr. Hunt's words can be borne by Mr. Chen or not, I certainly dare not be assertive. At least, I resolutely acknowledge that Mr. Chen's small "Oath" is a mature collection of poems.

In terms of quantity, it is certainly not a grand spectacle. One can finish reading the entire collection in under ten minutes with a quiet mind. Originally, there were many cases abroad where a single great poem caused a sensation in the entire literary world, so

Page 22

we should only pay attention to the quality of the poems, and the quantity of poems will not hinder the content of the poem. Chen's "Oath" only includes "Hesitation," "Night Walker," "I Feel Light All Over," "The Evening Breeze Blows Your White Dress," "You Must Not Have," "Oath," "I Say Goodbye to You," "I Visited My Lover's Home Today," "I Often Want to Think Like This," "Just See You Again," "The Moon is So Bright," and "Grave Door of Love," a total of twelve poems. Each poem, of course, has its independence and its own style. After reading them, it is as if we first eat jujubes and then suddenly taste the deliciousness of fresh lychees. Although the things eaten are different, the beauty of the taste has a consistent unity. That is to say, the style of the poem can be created by the author's artistic skills, but the different styles expressed all represent the author himself. Readers can easily feel a new excitement after reading, and singing it has a special interest, without feeling tired after reading at all, just wanting to read it continuously. A poem that can absorb the reader's heart is undoubtedly a poem worth singing again and again. If these twelve poems are combined in order, it is an extremely perfect long poem, and also the "oath" issued by the author to a woman.

Now, let's look at the different styles expressed in the author's poems.

I say goodbye to you,

"I'm leaving."

You close your mouth tightly,

Do not answer,

Ah, you close your mouth tightly,

Do not answer,

I say goodbye to you,

"I'm leaving." (I Say Goodbye to You)

My heart is just afraid,

Your house is dark and big, but also quaint,

Hanging a few calligraphy and paintings, the bottle is also inserted with wintersweet,

My heart is just afraid, (I Visited My Lover's Home Today using this format to write poetry can be said to be the author's creation. The words and sentences are extremely ordinary. In fact, this ordinariness contains a clear and simple beauty that other poets cannot write. In terms of rhythm, the author is also very attentive, but it also tends to be natural and not contrived, and often uses the same words for rhyme. This is also the author's unique creation.

The author also has a Nietzschean world-weary color. Because of unrequited love, in the poem "Love's Tomb Door," there is such an ending, "Just in this," this dim moonlight dusk, I am going, going to knock on the tomb door of love." This actually represents the author's own conclusion about love. Actually, entering the "Love's Tomb Door" is still hypocrisy and emptiness. Originally, love is essentially such a thing. In this point, the author is only passive, and will not conclusively solve the only direction after unrequited love is how. If you want to obtain the true fruit of love, it is definitely not something that can be seen by entering the "Love's Tomb Door". I believe that the author must strive to move forward in the future, and do not think that losing love means sacrificing everything of your own. Obviously, sacrificing everything of your own will not get a corresponding price. This is just that the author has not obtained an upward central consciousness, which of course does not have the slightest hindrance to the essence of the poem.

In terms of skills, there is no need to say that the author has achieved an unusual success. Each poem expresses a rare maturity. If the author can work hard to promote the poetry of the Chinese national spirit, and write it down in this style containing clear and simple beauty, and instill it into the folk, it will definitely achieve amazing results. At the same time, I dare to believe that the author's writing will definitely be greater than the so-called unrequited love poems that have been published now, because the author also has considerable research on children's poetry, and a little bit can be seen in the "Oath" collection of poems, otherwise, the author's poems will not have such natural rhythms and clear understanding in every poem.

On the recent extremely lonely poetry scene in China, the discovery of such a collection of poems is indeed worthy of our attention. Now, I have only written down what I felt after reading this collection of poems and introduced it to the readers. I believe you will also be sympathetic.

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest domestic and foreign publications. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc. are included in the introduction, but boring books will not be introduced.

Pictures are limited to the latest works of new domestic and foreign writers and accompanying pictures related to the text.
